The Father purposed, the Son accomplished, and the Spirit applies what the Son has accomplished and what the Father has purposed. The three work together as one.
The Father, the Son, and the Spirit Are Economically Three but One in Harmony
The Father, the Son, and the Spirit are essentially one but economically three. They are one in essence and three for economy. Yet They are still one in harmony in the economical Trinity (John 10:30; 17:21, 23). They are not in discord; They work in harmony. The three of the economical Trinity are the first "vital group" in the universe. We should model our vital groups after the three who are essentially one and work together as one in harmony. The harmony of the economical Trinity is evidenced by the picture in Matthew 3: The Father spoke in heaven concerning the Son, the Son stood in the water on the earth, and the Spirit soared as the dove in the air (vv. 16-17). This picture shows us that God is economically three. The harmony of the economical Trinity is also evidenced by the blessing of the Triune God in Ephesians 1: The Father chose the believers before the foundation of the world, the Son redeemed them in time, and the Spirit sealed them after they believed in the Son (vv. 4, 6-7, 13).
The Divine Trinity, the Triune God, is a mystery. We must accept the truth of the Triune God which is only according to the Bible's pure revelation and not what is according to traditional theology. The very Triune God is not for theology but for our experience. The processed and consummated Triune God is absolutely related to His economy to dispense Himself into His believers that they may be one in Him. We must bear this in mind as we touch the truth of the Triune God. Praise the Lord for His recovery! God does not need to be recovered, but the lost truth concerning the Triune God needs to be recovered. Because of our brother's faithful labor and sacrifice, this great truth in the Bible has been recovered to us. We have to testify that what is in the outline of this message is the crystallization of this great and mysterious truth. May we get into it and enjoy it.—M. C.
THE DIVINE TRINITY IS FOR THE DISPENSING OF GOD INTO HIS CHOSEN PEOPLE
We are thankful that we have received the truth of the Triune God, which is so lacking in today's Christianity. Our God is three, and yet He is one. Even as the economical Trinity He works as one in harmony. The Divine Trinity is for the dispensing of God into His chosen people. The Triune God is three-one for our benefit, so that He can dispense Himself into us, His chosen ones. We are those who have been chosen by Him, and He is triune to carry out His dispensing into us, not for our theological study but for us to experience Him in His dispensing.
The Triune God's Eternal Economy Is to Make Man the Same as He Is in Life and Nature but Not in His Godhead, and Thus to Be Enlarged and Expanded in His Expression
The Triune God's eternal economy according to His heart's desire is to make man the same as He is in life and nature but not in His Godhead, and thus to be enlarged and expanded in His expression. God has such a heart's desire to make us the same as He is. Of course, we are not the same as He is in His Godhead to be an object of worship, but we are exactly the same as He is in life and nature. We are God's kind and God's species. Christ is the God-man, and we have been made God-men. We are the real God-men, who are the same as He is in life and in nature. It is not a small thing to say this. When our brother began to point out these things, there was much opposition against this unveiling, especially from God's enemy. However, our brother was faithful to speak the high truth because he realized that God's desire in His trinity is to dispense Himself into all of us, God's chosen ones.
This Is Accomplished by Many Steps in His Economy
This is accomplished by creating man in His image and after His likeness (Gen. 1:26-27), becoming a man in His incarnation to partake of the human nature (Heb. 2:14a), living a human life to express His attributes through man's virtues, dying an all-inclusive death, resurrecting to become the firstborn Son of God and the life-giving Spirit (Rom. 8:29; Acts 13:33; 1 Cor. 15:45), dispensing Himself into God's chosen people to regenerate them with Himself as their life for producing many sons (1 Pet. 1:3), forming the churches with His many sons, and building up the Body of Christ with His brothers as the members to be the organism of the processed and consummated Triune God to consummate the New Jerusalem as His eternal enlargement and expression.
God first of all created man in His image and after His likeness so that man could express Him and represent Him. However, man fell, so God Himself became a man in His incarnation to partake of the human nature. Christ shared in flesh and blood just as we do, and in His living He lived a human life to express God's attributes through His human virtues. Christ's human living was God manifested in the flesh, and in this living He lived a life full of aromatic virtues. These aromatic virtues expressed God in all of His divine attributes so that whatever God is was expressed in this man. Because He put on flesh and blood just as we have, He was able to carry out the processes to accomplish God's eternal economy. He died an all-inclusive death, reconciling all things to Himself and taking care of all the problems that we had with God due to the fall. He not only took care of the problems, but He released His life through His death. His death was a life-releasing death so that He could be the one grain falling into the ground to die to bring forth many grains by dispensing Himself into us. Christ died, released His life, and then dispensed this life into His chosen ones.
Furthermore, in His resurrection He became something else. Up to that point He was God in the flesh, but on the day of His resurrection He was begotten to be the firstborn Son of God. He also became the pneumatic Christ, the life-giving Spirit, so that He could dispense Himself into His chosen people to regenerate them with Himself as their life for producing many sons. According to the pure revelation of the Bible, in 1 Peter 1:3, we were regenerated by the dispensing of the Triune God in the resurrection of Christ. These are the facts concerning Christ's resurrection.
God's goal in His trinity is to carry out His heart's desire to dispense Himself into His chosen ones, forming the churches with the many sons whom He regenerated. With all the churches that are formed with His many sons, He produces the one unique Body of Christ, with His brothers as the members, to be the organism of the processed and consummated Triune God. We are thankful to be His many sons and to be in the churches. However, at this particular time we are especially thankful that there is one organism, one Body, in the whole universe. Although we are in many churches, and although we are many members in the many churches, there is one unique expression on the whole earth, which is the Body of Christ. If we have seen the Body, there will be no problems in the Lord's recovery. We have been regenerated, we are the many members, His sons, and we have been produced as the churches. In all of the churches may we have such a realization that we are a part of the one unique organism, the Body of Christ, so that throughout the whole earth there can be one expression of Christ. If we are the Body of Christ in reality, this organism will consummate as the New Jerusalem, His eternal enlargement and expression. God's heart's desire is accomplished first through His creation, then through His incarnation, human living, all-inclusive death, and life-dispensing resurrection to produce the many sons and the churches to be the one organic Body of Christ to express Him and to consummate the New Jerusalem. This is the realization into which this ministry has brought us.
To Carry Out His Dispensing, God Needs to Be Triune
To carry out His dispensing, God needs to be triune. Our Triune God is the dispensing One. The Father as the origin is the fountain of living waters (Jer. 2:13). The Son as the expression is the spring (John 4:14). When He spoke with the woman at the well, the Son, the very embodiment and expression of God, referred to Himself as a spring. If we drink of Him, there is a spring of living water within us gushing up into eternal life. The Spirit as the transmission is the flow—the river (Rev. 22:1)—the reaching and the application of the Triune God. He is the fountain, the spring, and the flow. As the origin, the expression, and the transmission, He is flowing out. What we are enjoying today is the dispensing of our Triune God. He is the Divine Trinity for the dispensing of Himself into His chosen people.
The Divine Trinity Is Not for the Doctrinal Understanding of Systematic Theology but for the Dispensing of God Himself into His Chosen People to Accomplish His Economy
Second Corinthians 13:14 says, "The grace of the Lord Jesus Christ and. the love of God and the fellowship of the Holy Spirit be with you all," showing that the Divine Trinity is not for the doctrinal understanding of systematic theology but for the dispensing of God Himself into His chosen people to accomplish His economy. Praise the Lord for such a view of the Triune God! The grace of Christ, the love of God, and the fellowship of the Holy Spirit are not for us to study, to try to gain some doctrinal theology or understanding, but for us to enjoy in order to enter into the dispensing of the Triune God. We are here today for this dispensing. Through the ministry of Brother Nee and Brother Lee, we have been able to receive the truth concerning the Triune God, God being one yet three, and we have also realized that He is triune so that He can dispense Himself into us. As we live Him out in all the churches, we experience this dispensing. He is the Divine Trinity for the dispensing of Himself into us as His chosen people.
GOD IN HIS DIVINE TRINITY IS AN INCORPORATION AND HE PASSED THROUGH ALL THE PROCESSES TO BE INCORPORATED WITH MAN
God in His Divine Trinity is an incorporation and He passed through all the processes to be incorporated with man to be an enlarged, universal, divine-human incorporation, consummating the New Jerusalem.
God in His Divine Trinity Is an Incorporation
God in His Divine Trinity is an incorporation. In John 14 one of the Lord's disciples came to Him and asked Him to show them the Father. The Lord's response was, "Have I been so long a time with you, and you have not known Me, Philip? He who has seen Me has seen the Father; how is it that you say, Show us the Father? Do you not believe that I am in the Father and the Father is in Me? The words that I say to you I do not speak from Myself, but the Father who abides in Me does His works. Believe Me that I am in the Father and the Father is in Me; but if not, believe because of the works themselves" (v. 9-11). The Triune God is an incorporation by coinhering mutually and by working together as one. Christ is in the Father and the Father is in Him, and He and the Father are in the Spirit. Moreover, They do not work apart from one another. They coinhere mutually, and They work together as one.
The Second of the Divine Trinity Became a Man and Passed through All the Processes for God's Enlarged Incorporation
The Triune God in eternity past held a council (Acts 2:23) to make a decision that the second among Them had to become a man and pass through the processes of human living, death, and resurrection so that all the redeemed and regenerated believers of God would be incorporated into God's incorporation to be an enlarged incorporation. The Triune God is an incorporation, but He had to pass through a process so that all of us could enter into this incorporation so that He could become an enlarged incorporation. In John 14:20 Christ says, "In that day you will know that I am in My Father, and you in Me, and I in you." This is the enlarged incorporation.
The Processed and Consummated Triune God and the Redeemed and Regenerated Believers Became an Enlarged, Universal, Divine-human Incorporation
The processed and consummated Triune God and the redeemed and regenerated believers became an enlarged, universal, divine-human incorporation in the resurrection of Christ, indicated by "in that day" (John 14:20), consummating the New Jerusalem as the corporate God—the enlargement, expansion, and expression of God. God as an incorporation, according to His eternal plan, desired for us to be brought into Him as an enlarged incorporation. How we thank the Lord for the light from the ministry that brought us into this revelation, enabling us to see that we have been brought into this divine-human incorporation to be His enlargement and expression for eternity. The Issue of Christ Being Glorified by the Father with the Divine Glory on page 26 says,
In this message we have been burdened to point out that Christ's glorification produced, an issue—an incorporation. According to the divine revelation in the Scriptures God's work in the universe is to complete His economy, and God's desire in His economy is to have a unique incorporation. This is His universal concern. Millions of Adam's descendants have become believers in Christ. God's intention is to incorporate Himself with all the believers of Christ into one incorporation. The three of the Divine Trinity are an incorporation by coinhering mutually and by working together as one. This means that the three of the Divine Trinity are an incorporation by what They are and by what They do. This is the beginning of the universal incorporation, an incorporation which started with God Himself. God's intention is that all the believers of Christ would be incorporated into His incorporation to be an enlarged incorporation. This enlarged incorporation is unveiled in John 14:16-20. May the Lord open our eyes to see that the Triune God, who is in Himself an incorporation, has incorporated all the believers of Christ into His unique, universal incorporation. This incorporation is the issue of Christ's glorification.
God is three, and yet He is one. He is the Divine Trinity for the dispensing of Himself into His chosen people so that we can express Him, be His universal enlargement, and be incorporated into Him in a divine and human incorporation for eternity. He is triune so that we can realize and experience Him in a real way through His dispensing and be brought into this universal incorporation with the Triune God. This is the intention of our Triune God.—J. D.

GENERAL SUBJECT
The Crucial Contents of God's New Testament Economy
Message Five
The All-inclusive Christ— the Centrality and Universality of God's New Testament Economy
纲目|对照-听抄-目录
I.　Christ has the preeminence, the first place, in all things—Col. 1:18:
A.　Christ has the preeminence in the Triune Godhead—the first, the Father, always exalts the Son, and the third, the Spirit, always testifies concerning the Son—Phil. 2:9; John 15:26:
1.　Christ has the first place in all things; for in Him all the fullness was pleased to dwell—Col. 1:18b-19.
2.　In Christ dwells all the fullness of the Godhead bodily—Col. 2:9; Phil. 3:21.
B.　In God's old creation, Christ is the Firstborn of all creation—Col. 1:15b.
C.　In God's new creation in resurrection, Christ is the Firstborn from the dead—Col. 1:18b.
D.　We can also see the preeminence of Christ in God's exaltation:
1.　Christ has been exalted to the right hand of God in the third heaven—Acts 2:33a; Eph. 1:19-20.
2.　In God's exaltation of Christ, He has been given to be Head over all things—Eph. 1:22b.
3.　God has also given Him the name which is above every name—Phil. 2:9b.
E.　Christ has the preeminence in the church, being the Head of the Body, the church—Col. 1:18a.
II.　Christ is everything to the believers for their enjoyment:
A.　Christ is the God-allotted portion to the saints:
1.　The Father has qualified us for a share of the allotted portion of the saints in the light—Col. 1:12.
2.　The phrase?theirs and ours?in 1 Corinthians 1:2 indicates that Christ as the all-inclusive One belongs to all the believers.
B.　Christ is our life—Col. 3:4a:
1.　Christ lives in us—Gal. 2:20a; 2 Cor. 13:5.
2.　Christ should be our living—Phil. 1:21a.
3.　Christ should be magnified in our body—Phil. 1:20b.
4.　Christ should be formed in us—Gal. 4:19.
5.　We need to grow up into Christ, the Head, in all things with the growth of God—Eph. 4:15b; Col. 2:19b.
6.　We have to grow to such an extent that we can be presented to God full-grown in Christ—Col. 1:28b; Eph. 4:13b.
C.　Christ is in us as the hope of glory—Col. 1:27b:
1.　The hope of our calling (Eph. 1:18b; 4:4b) is the hope of glory, which is the transfiguration of our body and the manifestation of the sons of God—Rom. 8:19, 23-25.
2.　"He will change my body like unto His own, / Wholly making me the same as He"—Hymns,?#948.
D.　Christ is our every necessity and our full enjoyment:
1.　Christ is our light—John 8:12.
2.　Christ is our spiritual food—John 6:51, 57b.
3.　Christ is our spiritual drink—1 Cor. 10:4.
4.　Christ is our breath—John 20:22.
5.　Christ is our clothing—Gal. 3:27.
6.　Christ is our dwelling place—John 15:7a.
7.　Christ is our enjoyment and rest—Col. 2:16-17; Matt. 11:28.
E.　Christ is our divine provision:
1.　Christ is God's power—1 Cor. 1:24a.
2.　Christ is God's wisdom—1 Cor. 1:24b; 30a.
3.　Christ is our righteousness.
4.　Christ is our sanctification.
5.　Christ is our redemption—1 Cor. 1:30b.
III.　Christ is everything to the church:
A.　Christ is the Head of the Body—Col. 1:18.
B.　Christ is the Body of the Head—1 Cor. 12:12.
C.　Christ is the foundation of the church—1 Cor. 3:11.
D.　Christ is the living stone, the cornerstone, and the topstone of the house of God, the church—1 Pet. 2:4-8; Eph. 2:20; Zech. 4:7.
E.　Christ is all the members of the new man—Col. 3:10-11.
IV.　Christ is the centrality and universality of God's New Testament economy—Col. 1:17.
V.　Christ is the reality of every section of the God-ordained way:
A.　Christ is the reality in the fulfilling of the New Testament priesthood of the gospel—Rom. 15:16; 1 Pet. 2:5, 9.
B.　Christ is the reality in the feeding of the new believers—John 21:15.
C.　Christ is the reality of the perfecting of the saints in the vital groups—Eph. 4:12; Heb. 10:24-25.
D.　Christ is the reality in the building up of the church, the Body of Christ, by prophesying in the bigger meetings of the church—1 Cor. 14:3-5.

TOP-纲目|对照-听抄-目录
　
　
第五篇　包罗万有的基督─神新约经纶的中心与普及
The All-inclusive Christ— the Centrality and Universality of God's New Testament Economy
纲目|outline-听抄-目录
壹　基督在凡事上居首位，居第一位─西一18：
I.　Christ has the preeminence, the first place, in all things—Col. 1:18:
一　在神格的三者中间，首位总是归于第二者，子─第一者，父，总是高举子；第三者，灵，总是为子作见证─腓二9，约十五26：
A.　Christ has the preeminence in the Triune Godhead—the first, the Father, always exalts the Son, and the third, the Spirit, always testifies concerning the Son—Phil. 2:9; John 15:26:
１　基督在凡事上居首位；因为一切的丰满，乐意居住在祂里面─西一18下～19。
1.　Christ has the first place in all things; for in Him all the fullness was pleased to dwell—Col. 1:18b-19.
２　神格一切的丰满都有形有体的居住在祂里面─西二9，腓三21。
2.　In Christ dwells all the fullness of the Godhead bodily—Col. 2:9; Phil. 3:21.
二　在神的旧造里，基督是一切受造之物的首生者─西一15下。
B.　In God's old creation, Christ is the Firstborn of all creation—Col. 1:15b.
三　在复活里神的新造中，基督是从死人中复活的首生者─西一18下。
C.　In God's new creation in resurrection, Christ is the Firstborn from the dead—Col. 1:18b.
四　我们也能看见基督在神的高举里居首位：
D.　We can also see the preeminence of Christ in God's exaltation:
１　基督已被高举到三层天上神的右边─徒二33上，弗一19～20。
1.　Christ has been exalted to the right hand of God in the third heaven—Acts 2:33a; Eph. 1:19-20.
２　在神对基督的高举里，基督已得作万有的头─弗一22下。
2.　In God's exaltation of Christ, He has been given to be Head over all things—Eph. 1:22b.
３　神也赐给祂那超乎万名之上的名─腓二9下。
3.　God has also given Him the name which is above every name—Phil. 2:9b.
五　基督在召会中居首位，是召会身体的头─西一18上。
E.　Christ has the preeminence in the church, being the Head of the Body, the church—Col. 1:18a.
贰　基督是信徒的一切，作他们的享受：
II.　Christ is everything to the believers for their enjoyment:
一　基督是神所分给众圣徒的分：
A.　Christ is the God-allotted portion to the saints:
１　父叫我们够资格在光中同得所分给众圣徒的分─西一12。
1.　The Father has qualified us for a share of the allotted portion of the saints in the light—Col. 1:12.
２　林前一章二节，“祂是他们的，也是我们的”这句话指明基督这包罗万有者，属于所有的信徒。
2.　The phrase?theirs and ours?in 1 Corinthians 1:2 indicates that Christ as the all-inclusive One belongs to all the believers.
二　基督是我们的生命─西三4上：
B.　Christ is our life—Col. 3:4a:
１　基督在我们里面活着─加二20上，林后十三5。
1.　Christ lives in us—Gal. 2:20a; 2 Cor. 13:5.
２　基督应当是我们的生活─腓一21上。
2.　Christ should be our living—Phil. 1:21a.
３　基督应当在我们的身体上显大─腓一20下。
3.　Christ should be magnified in our body—Phil. 1:20b.
４　基督应当成形在我们里面─加四19。
4.　Christ should be formed in us—Gal. 4:19.
５　我们需要在凡事上以神的增长而长到元首基督里面─弗四15下，西二19下。
5.　We need to grow up into Christ, the Head, in all things with the growth of God—Eph. 4:15b; Col. 2:19b.
６　我们必须长大到一个地步，使我们能在基督里成熟的献给神─西一28下，弗四13下。
6.　We have to grow to such an extent that we can be presented to God full-grown in Christ—Col. 1:28b; Eph. 4:13b.
三　基督在我们里面是荣耀的盼望─西一27下：
C.　Christ is in us as the hope of glory—Col. 1:27b:
１　我们呼召的盼望（弗一18下，四4下）是荣耀的盼望，就是我们的身体改变形状，以及神的众子显示出来─罗八19，23～25。
1.　The hope of our calling (Eph. 1:18b; 4:4b) is the hope of glory, which is the transfiguration of our body and the manifestation of the sons of God—Rom. 8:19, 23-25.
２　“还要改变我体，和祂体相同，使我完全与祂像符合”─诗歌七六四首。
2.　"He will change my body like unto His own, / Wholly making me the same as He"—Hymns,?#948.
四　基督是我们每一种需要和完全的享受：
D.　Christ is our every necessity and our full enjoyment:
１　基督是我们的光─约八12。
1.　Christ is our light—John 8:12.
２　基督是我们的灵食─约六51，57下。
2.　Christ is our spiritual food—John 6:51, 57b.
３　基督是我们的灵水─林前十4。
3.　Christ is our spiritual drink—1 Cor. 10:4.
４　基督是我们的气息─约二十22。
4.　Christ is our breath—John 20:22.
５　基督是我们的衣服─加三27。
5.　Christ is our clothing—Gal. 3:27.
６　基督是我们的居所─约十五7上。
6.　Christ is our dwelling place—John 15:7a.
７　基督是我们的享受和安息─西二16～17，太十一28。
7.　Christ is our enjoyment and rest—Col. 2:16-17; Matt. 11:28.
五　基督是我们神圣的供备：
E.　Christ is our divine provision:
１　基督是神的能力─林前一24上。
1.　Christ is God's power—1 Cor. 1:24a.
２　基督是神的智慧─林前一24下，30上。
2.　Christ is God's wisdom—1 Cor. 1:24b; 30a.
３　基督是我们的公义。
3.　Christ is our righteousness.
４　基督是我们的圣别。
4.　Christ is our sanctification.
５　基督是我们的救赎─林前一30下。
5.　Christ is our redemption—1 Cor. 1:30b.
叁　基督是召会的一切：
III.　Christ is everything to the church:
一　基督是身体的头─西一18。
A.　Christ is the Head of the Body—Col. 1:18.
二　基督是头的身体─林前十二12。
B.　Christ is the Body of the Head—1 Cor. 12:12.
三　基督是召会的根基─林前三11。
C.　Christ is the foundation of the church—1 Cor. 3:11.
四　基督是神的家（召会）的活石、房角石和顶石─彼前二4～8，弗二20，亚四7。
D.　Christ is the living stone, the cornerstone, and the topstone of the house of God, the church—1 Pet. 2:4-8; Eph. 2:20; Zech. 4:7.
五　基督是新人一切的肢体─西三10～11。
E.　Christ is all the members of the new man—Col. 3:10-11.
肆　基督是神新约经纶的中心与普及─西一17。
IV.　Christ is the centrality and universality of God's New Testament economy—Col. 1:17.
伍　基督是神命定之路每一段的实际：
V.　Christ is the reality of every section of the God-ordained way:
一　在履行新约福音祭司的职任上，基督是实际─罗十五16，彼前二5，9。
A.　Christ is the reality in the fulfilling of the New Testament priesthood of the gospel—Rom. 15:16; 1 Pet. 2:5, 9.
二　在喂养初信者的事上，基督是实际─约二一15。
B.　Christ is the reality in the feeding of the new believers—John 21:15.
三　在活力排中成全圣徒的事上，基督是实际─弗四12，来十24～25。
C.　Christ is the reality of the perfecting of the saints in the vital groups—Eph. 4:12; Heb. 10:24-25.
四　在召会较大的聚会中申言以建造召会，基督身体的事上，基督是实际─林前十四3～5。
D.　Christ is the reality in the building up of the church, the Body of Christ, by prophesying in the bigger meetings of the church—1 Cor. 14:3-5.

TOP-纲目|outline-听抄-目录
　
　
MESSAGE FIVE
THE ALL-INCLUSIVE CHRIST— THE CENTRALITY AND UNIVERSALITY OF GOD'S NEW TESTAMENT ECONOMY
纲目|Outline|对照-目录
（本文为英文听抄扫描所得，未经校对）
The all-inclusive Christ is the centrality and universality of God's New Testament economy. The all-inclusive Christ is the content of the apostles' teaching and the focus and essence of the New Testament ministry. He is also the embodiment of the processed, consummated, and dispensing Triune God. Under the ministry in the Lord's recovery we have been brought to this dear, precious, preeminent, enjoyable, all-inclusive Christ. Hearing about this Christ year after year under this ministry has made us crazy lovers of Jesus.
That Christ is all-inclusive means that everything is included in Him. Christ is both God and man, the God-man, the complete God and the perfect man. As the all-inclusive One, He passed through incarnation to become the God-man, who lived the most attractive, captivating, and aromatic human living ever lived in the universe. This God-man possesses both divinity and humanity. In His humanity He accomplished His all-inclusive, judicial redemption through His marvelous death, and in His divinity He is carrying out His organic salvation through His life-dispensing, life-giving resurrection. The resurrection is not merely a two-thousand-year-old historical fact; it is included in the all-inclusive Christ. In resurrection our Christ became a life-giving Spirit so that He can enter into us to make us part of the new creation in His resurrection. Included in this Christ is also His glorious ascension, in which He was made the Lord, the Christ, and the Head over all things to the church. That Christ is all-inclusive means that He is everything. He is everything in the apostles' teaching and in the New Testament ministry, and He is the centrality and the universality in God's economy. From the center to the circumference, Christ is everything in God's economy. He is the hub, the spokes, and the rim. Christ is our enjoyment and our joy, and He is the reality of every positive thing in the entire universe. He is everything. This is the precious Christ to whom we have been betrothed through the ministry. We stand in deep appreciation with an eternal gratitude to Brother Lee for betrothing us to this dear, all-inclusive Christ. On March 22, 1997 Brother Lee wrote a letter of fellowship with thanks to the churches, whom he addressed in this way:
To all of my fellow participants in the Lords recovery, who love the ministry, who enjoy and share the unsearchable riches of the all-inclusive Christ through the ministry, and who are willing to pay the price to seek, gain, and follow the Lord Jesus, whom we love, and bear His reproach outside the camp.
He signed the letter, "Your fellow partaker in experiencing and gaining Christ." Our brother was a lover of Christ, and all he did was minister Christ to us. Two of the six chapters of The Ten Great Critical "Ones" for the Building Up of the Body of Christ, from messages spoken in October 1995 on the truths in the Lord's recovery, are on Christ, the unsearchable One. Page 33 says, "The Lord's recovery is the recovery of Christ." We are glad to be in the Lord's recovery, which is a recovery not merely of matters, things, places, and items, but of the dear, marvelous, all-inclusive Christ, who is the centrality and universality of God's economy.
CHRIST HAS THE PREEMINENCE, THE FIRST PLACE, IN ALL THINGS
Christ has the preeminence, the first place, in all things (Col. 1:18). Christ having the preeminence is vitally related to His being everything to the believers for their enjoyment. If we see that Christ is preeminent and has the first place in all things, and if we practice to honor Him as such, the Lord's recovery has a bright future. Every one of us will be full of the sevenfold intensified enjoyment of the all-inclusive Christ. Christ's being everything to us hinges on His having the preeminence.
Among the Three in the Godhead, the Preeminence Always Goes to the Second, the Son
Among the three in the Godhead, the preeminence always goes to the second, the Son. Christ has the preeminence in the Triune Godhead—the first, the Father, always exalts the Son, and the third, the Spirit, always testifies concerning the Son (Phil. 2:9; John 15:26). Philippians 2:8-9 says that after Christ humbled Himself and became obedient to death, even the death of the cross, God highly exalted Him. The Father has exalted the Son. In Matthew 3:17 at the Lord's baptism and in 17:5 on the Mount of Transfiguration, the Father spoke, "This is My Son, the Beloved, in whom I have found My delight." This was the Father's giving the preeminence to the Son. John 15:26 tells us that the Spirit is the Spirit of reality to make everything of Christ real to us, applied to us, and experienced by us. In this way He always testifies concerning the Son. If both the Father and the Spirit exalt the Son, we must also exalt the Son. The best way to honor the Father and take care of the Spirit is to enjoy the Son, praise the Son, be under the Son, and give Him His rightful position. Christ must have the preeminence.
Christ Has the First Place in All Things; For in Him All the Fullness Was Pleased to Dwell
Christ has the first place in all things; for in Him all the fullness was pleased to dwell (Col. l:18b-19). This mysterious phrase tells us that the fullness is a person; the fullness was pleased. God in the riches of His expression is pleased to dwell in Christ. That the fullness was pleased to dwell in Christ shows that Christ is the preeminent One in the Triune Godhead.
In Christ Dwells All the Fullness of the Godhead Bodily
In Christ dwells all the fullness of the Godhead bodily (Col. 2:9; Phil. 3:21). Not only is the fullness pleased to dwell in Christ, but in Christ's incarnation, in His becoming a man by putting on the flesh, all the fullness of the Triune Godhead was pleased to dwell within this God-man bodily, physically. This also strengthens the fact that Christ has the preeminence in the Triune Godhead. The Father exalts the Son, and the Spirit testifies concerning the Son, so our life must be a life of exalting the Son. That is why we love to say, "Lord Jesus, I love You." When we consider Brother Lee's life, we can see that he was a lover of Christ, always exalting the Son, praising the Son, recognizing His preeminence, coming under Him, and giving Him the preeminence in his ministry.
In God's Old Creation, Christ Is the Firstborn of All Creation, and in God's New Creation in Resurrection, Christ Is the Firstborn from the Dead
In God's old creation, Christ is the Firstborn of all creation (Col. 1:15b), and in God's new creation in resurrection, Christ is the Firstborn from the dead (v. 18b). In both the old creation and the new creation, Christ has the preeminence. Colossians 1:15 says that Christ "is the image of the invisible God, the Firstborn of all creation." The word Firstborn implies preeminence, and it leads us to the clear realization that Christ is everything in creation. Verses 16-17 say, "Because in Him all things were created, in the heavens and on the earth, the visible and the invisible, whether thrones or lordships or rulers or authorities; all things have been created through Him and unto Him. And He is before all things, and all things cohere in Him." The whole creation is in Him, through Him, and unto Him. Moreover, He is the intrinsic power, the active instrument, and the consummation of the entire old creation. Since the entire old creation coheres in Him, He certainly is the preeminent One in the old creation.
Verse 18 says, "And He is the Head of the Body, the church; He is the beginning, the Firstborn from the dead, that He Himself might have the first place in all things." We love such a One and we want Him to have the first place in each of us. He holds the preeminence within the Triune Godhead, and He is preeminent in the old creation and in the new creation in resurrection, which includes us. Our experience and enjoyment of Him have much to do with the recognition of the fact that Christ has the preeminence. The Life-study of Colossians on page 42 says,
He is the first both in creation and in resurrection. This means that He is the first in the old creation, the universe, and in the new creation, the church. The universe is the environment in which the church exists as the Body of Christ to express Christ in full. Christ is not only first in the church, the Body, but also first in the environment, the universe. This means that He is first in everything.
We Can Also See the Preeminence of Christ in God's Exaltation
We can see also the preeminence of Christ in God's exaltation. Christ has been exalted to the right hand of God in the third heaven (Acts 2:33a; Eph. 1:19-20). In God's exaltation of Christ, He has been given to be Head over all things to the church (v. 22b). God has also given Him the name which is above every name. Philippians 2:9-11 says, "Therefore also God highly exalted Him and bestowed on Him the name which is above every name, that in the name of Jesus every knee should bow, of those who are in heaven and on earth and under the earth, and every tongue should topenly confess that Jesus Christ is Lord to the glory of God the Father." God the Father is pleased when we exalt the Son by confessing that Jesus Christ is Lord.
Christ Has the Preeminence in the Church, Being the Head of the Body, the Church
Christ has the preeminence in the church, being the Head of the Body, the church (Col. 1:18a). Christs being the Head over all things to the church implies a transmission. Every time we recognize His preeminence, come under His headship, enthrone Him on our praises, confess His name, and tell Him that we love Him, we enter into the enjoyment of His transmission, and He becomes our real portion in every way.
Psalms 73—76 speak of the desolation of God's house and Christ as the solution. Concerning this, Christ and the Church Revealed and Typified in the Psalms shows us that the maintenance, restoration, and going on of the Lord's testimony have altogether to do with the position Christ is given among God's people. Giving Christ the preeminence, the headship, and the first place in all things is very critical. When Christ is given His rightful place in the Lord's recovery, we have no problems. In order for the Lord to prevail and have a way in His recovery at this critical time, we must receive this word with our entire being, recognizing that Christ must have the preeminence in all things. Our daily life should be a life of praying, "Lord, I am nothing; I am nobody. You are the preeminent One. You are everything." Philippians 4:2 records that two sisters were contending with each other. What they both needed was to bow their knees and pray in this way. By our giving Christ the preeminence, all the problems are solved; He is the unique solution to all the problems. That is why Paul told the Philippians, "Rejoice in the Lord always; again I will say, rejoice" (v. 4). When we rejoice in the Lord, we give Him the preeminence, but if Christ is not given His rightful place, God's house enters into desolation. May the Lord preserve us from such desolation. In the same way, those who are considering marriage must know that if Christ is not given the preeminence, their marriage will result in manipulating and maneuvering, but the more we enjoy the Lord and give Him the first place, the more He has a way in our human living, and all things turn out for good for His eternal economy.
CHRIST IS EVERYTHING TO THE BELIEVERS FOR THEIR ENJOYMENT Christ Is the God-allotted Portion to the Saints
Christ is everything to the believers for their enjoyment. Colossians 1:12 tells us that Christ is the God-allotted portion to the saints. He is our God-allotted portion for us to enjoy. The Father is the One who has put Christ on us as our robe through the redeeming death of the Son. He has qualified us to enjoy Christ as the fatted calf and the all-inclusive good land.
The Father Has Qualified Us for a Share of the Allotted Portion of the Saints in the Light
The Father has qualified us for a share of the allotted portion of the saints in the light. The phrase in the light has much to do with our enjoyment of Christ. Many times we do not enjoy Christ because we have turned away from Him, but as we turn our heart back to Him and come into His presence with His shining, we repent and confess, "Lord, I left You. I was away from You." At that time, our enjoyment begins afresh. Christ becomes our fresh, enjoyable, God-allotted portion. In a certain room there may be food to eat and nice things to enjoy, but if the room is in darkness, we cannot enjoy those things. To enjoy Christ, we have to enjoy Him in the light, turning our heart to Him and coming forward into His presence. We need to be under His shining and be quick to repent. If brothers are about to argue with each other, they need to turn to the Lord, get into His shining, confess, repent, and give Him the preeminence. In this way, we enjoy Him as our God-allotted portion.
The Phrase Theirs and Ours in 1 Corinthians 1:2 Indicates That Christ as the All-inclusive One Belongs to All the Believers
The phrase theirs and ours in 1 Corinthians 1:2 indicates that Christ as the all-inclusive One belongs to all the believers. Verse 9 says, "God is faithful, through whom you were called into the fellowship of His Son, Jesus Christ our Lord." Christ is our all-inclusive enjoyment; He is our portion. Verse 2 speaks of "our Lord Jesus Christ...who is theirs and ours." Christ is possessable. He is "theirs" in Moscow, and "ours" in Anaheim. Wherever we are, He is our portion.
Christ Is Our Life
Christ is our life (Col. 3:4a). That Christ is our life means that He has become us. Nothing can be closer to us than our life. If we realize that Christ is our life, we will shout one million hallelujahs. Christ lives in us (Gal. 2:20a; 2 Cor. 13 5) When we drive on the freeway, He drives in us. If we realize this, our driving will be different. We will have much enjoyment of Christ throughout the day. Christ should be our living (Phil. 1:21a), and Christ should be magnified in our body (v. 20b). Those who were with Brother Lee can testify that even up to his death Christ was magnified in him whether through life or through death. For Christ to be magnified means that He is made larger through a God-man with a God-man living. We all need to grow up into Christ.
Christ should be formed in us (Gal. 4:19), and we need to grow up into Christ, the Head, in all things with the growth of God (Eph. 4:15b; Col. 2:19b). We have to grow to such an extent that we can be presented to God full-grown in Christ (Col. 1:28b; Eph. 4:13b). To be full-grown in Christ means that we become Him in life. For us to become the Body of Christ and the bride of Christ requires that we give Him the preeminence in all things and that He be everything to us for our enjoyment.—D. T.
Christ Is in Us as the Hope of Glory
The Hope of Our Calling Is the Hope of Glory
Christ is in us as the hope of glory. Colossians 1:27 speaks of "Christ in you, the hope of glory." The hope of our calling (Eph. 1:18b; 4:4b) is the hope of glory, which is the transfiguration of our body and the manifestation of the sons of God (Rom. 8:19, 23-25). We are people full of hope, but our hope is not in the things that the worldly people hope for. People in the world hope for money, better houses, and many vain things. We, however, should have no hope other than the hope of glory, which is Christ in us.
"He Will Change My Body Like unto His Own"
The second verse of Hymns, #948, which was written by Brother Lee, says, "In my spirit He regenerated me, / In my soul He's now transforming me. / He will change my body like unto His own, / Wholly making me the same as He." The hope of glory is that we will be changed to be the same as He. Speaking of the hope of glory, Romans 8:18-19 says, "For I consider that the sufferings of this present time are not worthy to be compared with the coming glory to be revealed upon us. For the anxious watching of the creation eagerly awaits the revelation of the sons of God." The revelation of the sons of God will take place when our body is transfigured, that is, when Christ in us is glorified in our body. Concerning the revelation of the sons of God, footnote 2 of verse 19 in the Recovery Version says,
An unveiling or appearing of something previously covered or hidden. Although we are the sons of God, we are veiled, not yet revealed. At the Lord's second coming, when we will be glorified and our bodies will be fully redeemed, the veil will be lifted. The creation is eagerly awaiting this. This revelation will be the consummation of the process of designation that we are now passing through (see note 41 in ch. 1).
Romans 1:4 says that the Lord Jesus was designated the Son of God in His resurrection. He was uplifted in His humanity to be the Son of God in His human nature. We also will be designated the sons of God. Our glorification will be our designation. We are sons of God today in our spirit, and our soul is being sonized, but no one can see the divine element in our body. At the time of our glorification, however, the process of designation will be fully completed, and the whole creation will realize that we are sons of God.
God's glorification of our mortal body will be the full redemption of our body. Christ will change our body like unto His own, wholly making us the same as He. Our spirit today contains God and is mingled with God, our soul is being deified, and in that day even our body will be brought into the divine glory. The glory of God within us will shine out through us. There is nothing better than to be one with God in spirit, soul, and body in order to become God in life, in nature, and even in appearance and expression, but not in the Godhead. This is the wonderful hope of our calling. All of creation is waiting for our designation.
Christ Is Our Every Necessity and Our Full Enjoyment
Christ is our every necessity and our full enjoyment. A very striking point of Brother Lee's ministry is that he helped us to learn to enjoy Christ. Most of us did not know how to enjoy Christ before we came under this ministry. Even the term enjoy Christ was like a foreign language to us, and even today it still is to many believers. They may know how to believe into Christ and trust in Christ, but they do not know what it is to enjoy Christ. The enjoyment of Christ is a hallmark of the New Testament ministry because God is dispensed into us by this enjoyment. According to God's sovereign ordination, we need to eat Christ and drink Christ for the maintenance of life and the increase of life. God is so sweet, so He makes the eating and the drinking very enjoyable. We enjoy all the necessities of life: eating, drinking, and breathing. In God's economy we enjoy God's dispensing by enjoying Christ. This is a major item in the Lord's recovery. Some believers have questioned whether it is right to enjoy God, but 1 Peter 2:3 tells us that we have "tasted that the Lord is good." We can taste that the Lord is good. He is so enjoyable. This is the way God is dispensed into us.
There is nothing as vital or as basic to our Christian life and to the church life as the real, practical enjoyment of Christ. This enjoyment is not Christ in doctrine or in knowledge but Christ in life, in the Spirit, and in reality. He is a living person for us to deal with. We can never graduate from enjoying Christ. This is our maintenance of life. We need the highest understanding, and the Lord has even given us the high peaks of the truth. However, no matter how high our understanding may be, we need to enjoy Christ and eat Christ in all of these peaks. The Lord is constantly giving us more ways to enjoy Him. We enjoy Him by calling on His name, by pray-reading His Word, and by praying, and now we are learning to enjoy Him by PSRP—pray-reading, studying, reciting, and prophesying. This is to enjoy Christ for His dispensing to fulfill God's economy.
Many Christians know the points in this portion of the message. We may know that Christ is our light and the bread of life, and we may even use these terms. However, even though we know that Christ is the living water, do we drink Him as the living water? Do we eat Christ as the bread of life and enjoy the light of life? To know these terms is one thing, but to enjoy Christ is another. In the Lord's recovery, may the Lord save us from falling into the realm of knowledge. We have to be the enjoyers of our Lord Jesus Christ.
Colossians 1:12 tells us that Christ is our portion, and 1 Corinthians 1:2 says that Christ is "theirs and ours." He is the portion of every believer. However, we still need the way to realize all the wonderful things concerning Christ and to enter into the experience of Him as our light, our food, and our drink. Therefore 1 Corinthians 15:45 tells us that this Christ, who is the portion allotted to us by God, became a life-giving Spirit. This is one of the most crucial truths in the entire New Testament. Merely to know that Christ is our life, our light, our drink, our food, our breath, and our clothing is wonderful, but we can get into the experience of these aspects because Christ today is pneumatic. He is the pneumatic Christ for us to enter into and for Him to enter into us. We can eat Him as food, and we can drink Him as drink. He can shine within us as the light of life. The key to the enjoyment of Christ is to know that today Christ is the life-giving Spirit. We can never graduate from this realization.
Christ Is Our Light
We enjoy Christ in so many aspects as our every necessity and our full enjoyment. First, Christ is our light (John 8:12). Life needs light. Christ being our life requires that we have Him as the light of life.
Christ Is Our Spiritual Food
Christ is our spiritual food (John 6:51, 57b). This is a great item in the Lords recovery. We need to eat Jesus every day, enjoy Him, and give Him. the preeminence that He can have the first place in all things. We cannot get away from this. He needs to have the preeminence in our day. The first thing we need to do after getting out of bed is to eat Jesus. We need to call on His name and get into His Word. Christ should have the preeminence in what we eat. We should not eat the newspaper or the radio after first rising up; we should eat Christ in His Word. We need to ask ourselves if we have spent time each day to eat the Lord. We never graduate from this. If we do graduate, we are finished. We will fall into oldness and deadness. Then we may have much knowledge, but we will be without the living experience of Christ. In John 6:57 the Lord said, "As the living Father has sent Me and I live because of the Father, so he who eats Me, he also shall live because of Me." If we want to live Christ, we have to eat Him. There is no way around this.
Christ Is Our Spiritual Drink
Christ is our spiritual drink (1 Cor. 10:4). Moses smote the rock in the wilderness, and out of it came water. This is a type, showing us that Christ is our drink. Those who are new in the Lords recovery and those who are experienced all have to drink Him. The best way to drink Him is to call on His name, saying, "Lord Jesus, I love You. I need You. O Lord Jesus. Hallelujah!" We never outgrow our need to drink. We need to begin every day by calling on the Lord. The first thing in the morning when we wake up, we have to call on the Lord a number of times to get out of our mind and into our spirit.
Christ Is Our Breath
Christ is our breath (John 20:22). This and the preceding items are for the maintenance of life. We never outgrow our need for light, food, drink, and breath. We breathe Him by calling and by praying. A wonderful hymn by A. B. Simpson says that we are breathing in of Christ and breathing out of our self. We breathe in by calling, and we breathe out by confessing. We should help the new ones among us not to pray long prayers but simply to call on the Lord, say something simple, and then call on the Lord again. Our prayer is not like a letter sent to Christ. Our prayer is our speaking to Him and breathing Him in at the same time.
Christ Is Our Clothing
Christ is our clothing. Galatians 3:27 says, "For as many as were baptized into Christ have put on Christ." We are clothed with Christ. This is an objective fact. We cannot see this clothing, but the angels see it, the devil sees it, and the demons see it. There is also the experiential aspect of Christ as our clothing. The more we enjoy Him, the more we are filled with Him and the more we can subjectively experience being covered with Christ in every way. In society, when we do not have the proper clothing for a certain occasion, we feel ashamed. In the same way, when we are away from the Lord, when we are not filled with Christ in our experience, we sense our shame and inadequacy; we sense that we are not properly clothed. We need to be filled with Christ and be clothed with Him.
Christ Is Our Dwelling Place
Christ is our dwelling place (John 15:7a). Moses said, "O Lord, You have been our dwelling place / In all generations" (Psa. 90:1). We all have to flee into our refuge, which is our spirit mingled with the pneumatic Christ. Christ is our dwelling place, our hiding place, and our refuge. Many times we sense that we are inadequate, but we have a hiding place. We can flee into Christ.
Christ Is Our Enjoyment and Rest
Christ is our enjoyment and rest (Col. 2:16-17). In Matthew 11:28-29 the Lord said, "Come to Me all who toil and are burdened, and I will give you rest. Take My yoke upon you and learn from Me, for I am meek and lowly in heart, and you will find rest for your souls." Sometimes when we rest our soul and body, we do not sense that we are at rest. If we do not labor to enjoy Christ, our rest is not a real rest. To have real rest is to enjoy and be satisfied with Christ. We need to learn of the Lord. He was a person who was fully satisfied with the Father's will, and He was a person at rest.
Christ Is Our Divine Provision
Christ is our divine provision. The crucified Christ is God's power and God's wisdom (1 Cor. 1:24, 30a). Christ is our righteousness, our sanctification, and our redemption. First Corinthians 1:30 speaks of Christ as our divine provision for our past, present, and future and for our spirit, soul, and body. Christ is our righteousness for the past so that we can be born of God in our spirit. Christ is our sanctification for the present so that our soul can be transformed with the element of Christ. Christ is our redemption for the future so that we may be redeemed in our body. Christ is God's divine provision for our regeneration, transformation, and glorification. All is of Christ. Therefore, verse 31 says, "He who boasts, let him boast in the Lord." We have nothing to boast of but Christ as our righteousness, sanctification, and redemption of our body.
CHRIST IS EVERYTHING TO THE CHURCH
Christ is everything to the church. Christ is the Head of the Body (Col. 1:18), and we must give Him the preeminence as the Head. On the one hand, He is the Head of the church, and on the other hand, He is the Head of each one of us. We are connected to the Head, and we need to grow up into the Head in all things. Furthermore, Christ is the Body of the Head (1 Cor. 12:12) and the foundation of the church (3:11). He is the living stone, the cornerstone, and the topstone of the house of God, the church (1 Pet. 2:4-8; Eph. 2:20; Zech. 4:7). He is the living stone, and He is making us living stones. He is the cornerstone joining the Jews and the Gentiles for the one building of God, and He is the topstone to complete God's building of His house. He is also a stone of stumbling to the Jews (Rom. 9:32-33) and a smiting stone to the nations (Matt. 21:44). Christ is a marvelous all-inclusive stone.
Christ Is All the Members of the New Man
Christ is all the members of the new man. Colossians 3:10-11 tells us that in the new man there is no room for any culture, race, nationality, social rank, or ethnic group. Christ is all the members and in all the members. In the church Christ is everything, and everything else is screened out.
CHRIST IS THE CENTRALITY AND UNIVERSALITY OF GOD'S NEW TESTAMENT ECONOMY
Christ is the centrality and universality of God's New Testament economy. Colossians 1:17 says that all things cohere in Him. Everything in the universe is held together in Christ. Scientists know that there is some kind of mysterious "glue" in this universe that holds everything together. They do not know what it is, but we know that the "glue" is Christ. He is the hub, He is the spokes, and He is the rim, and all things cohere in Him. On the one hand, this is true in a universal sense, but on the other hand, we need to apply this truth in a particular way: Our family life coheres in Christ, our marriage coheres in Him, and the church in our locality coheres in Him. If we experience Christ, everything is held together and subsists in Him.
CHRIST IS THE REALITY OF EVERY SECTION OF THE GOD-ORDAINED WAY
Christ is the reality of every section of the God-ordained way. Christ is the reality in the fulfilling of the New Testament priesthood of the gospel (Rom. 15:16; 1 Pet. 2:5, 9). Our gospel preaching is not an empty preaching. It brings the Christ whom we enjoy and experience to people. Christ is also the reality in the feeding and shepherding of the new believers (John 21:15). Our feeding feeds people with Christ, and our shepherding is "according to God" (1 Pet. 5:2). Christ is our shepherding. The new way is not merely a way. The new way is a person. Christ is the gospel, and Christ is the great Shepherd and chief Shepherd among us.
Christ is the reality of the perfecting of the saints in the vital groups (Eph. 4:12; Heb. 10:24-25). He is perfecting us through the gifted members. This perfecting is not something outside of Christ. Christ is the reality in the building up of the church, the Body of Christ, by prophesying in the bigger meetings of the church (1 Cor. 14:3-5). To prophesy is to speak forth Christ. When we speak, we speak Christ for the building up. In everything Christ is our enjoyment. Christ is all-inclusive, and we need to give Him the preeminence.—C. J.

TOP-纲目|Outline|对照-目录
　
　
第六篇　基督在三个时期中丰满的职事─成肉体、总括与加强
大纲|Outline|对照-听抄-目录
壹　基督丰满职事的第一个时期，是祂成肉体的时期，就是基督在肉体里的时期，从祂的出生，经过祂的人性生活，到祂的死：
一　在祂的成肉体里，基督将无限的神带到有限的人里面；祂也将三一神与三部分人联结并调和一起。
二　在祂的人性生活里，基督借着祂芬芳的美德，在祂的人性里彰显全备之神丰富的属性：
１　基督在祂人性生活中彰显全备的神，主要的是彰显神丰富的属性。
２　基督借着祂芬芳的美德吸引并夺取人：
a　不是在祂的肉体里，凭祂人性的生命活着。
b　乃是在祂的复活中，凭祂神圣的生命活着。
三　在祂的死里，基督完成祂包罗万有之法理的救赎：
１　祂了结一切旧造的东西。
２　祂救赎神所创造、却堕落在罪中的一切东西─来二9，西一20。
３　祂用祂神圣的元素创造（孕育）新人─弗二15。
４　祂从祂人性的体壳里，将祂神圣的生命释放出来─约十二24。
５　祂为祂生机的救恩立下根基，并且设定达成祂在总括时期中之职事的手续。
贰　基督丰满职事的第二个时期，是祂总括的时期，就是基督成为赐生命之灵的时期，从祂的复活到召会的堕落：
一　在祂的复活中，基督生为神的长子─徒十三33：
１　从已过无始的永远，基督就是神的独生子，只具有神性，并无人性，也没有经过死而进入复活。
２　神的独生子在成肉体时，化身成为一个神人，就是一个兼有神人二性的人。
３　基督在肉体里作大卫的后裔，借着死与复活，被标出为神的儿子─罗一3～4：
a　在死里，祂的人性被钉十字架。
b　在复活中，祂被钉死的人性被祂神性的灵所点活，（彼前三18，）并且被提高到神独生子之儿子名分里。─引用经文
c　因此，祂在复活中被神生为神的长子。
二　在祂的复活中，末后的亚当基督成为赐生命的灵─林前十五45下：
１　神的儿子基督，就是神圣三一的第二者，完成祂在地上的职事之后，在复活中成了，就是改变形状而成为赐生命的灵。
２　基督成为赐生命的灵，乃是为要将那局限在基督人性体壳里的神圣生命释放出来，并将其分赐到祂的信徒里面，使他们成为构成祂身体的许多肢体─约十二24。
３　这赐生命的灵就是那是灵的基督，也称为生命的灵，（罗八2，）耶稣的灵，（徒十六7，）基督的灵，（罗八9，）耶稣基督的灵，（腓一19，）主灵。（林后三18）。─引用经文
三　在祂的复活中，基督为着祂的身体重生信徒─彼前一3：
１　那是灵的基督成了神的长子和赐生命的灵，为着重生信徒，使他们成为神的许多儿子，与祂在一个宇宙的大生产中一同由神所生：
a　为着组成神的家，就是神的家人。
b　为着构成基督的身体作祂的丰满，就是祂的彰显和扩展，以完成经过过程并终极完成之三一神永远的彰显和扩展。
２　基督在复活里借着说神的话，没有限量的将祂自己这包罗万有、赐生命的灵赐给人─约三34。
３　所有在基督里的信徒都被建造，成为神在他们由祂的灵内住之灵里的居所，（弗二22，）这乃是借着在性质上的圣别、（罗十五16、）更新、（多三5、）变化、（林后三18）和模成。（罗八29。）─引用经文
叁　基督丰满职事的第三个时期，是祂加强的时期，就是基督是七倍加强之灵的时期，从召会的堕落到新耶路撒冷的终极完成：
一　基督在祂职事的第三个时期中所作的第一件事，就是加强祂生机的救恩：
１　基督在祂总括时期中，要完成祂生机的救恩，为着产生召会，建造基督的身体，以终极完成新耶路撒冷，但在这时期之职事的中途，召会堕落了，阻扰神永远经纶的完成。
２　因此，基督成了七倍加强的灵，（启一4，四5，五6，三1，）要七倍的加强神生机的救恩，为着建造基督的身体，以终极完成神永远的目标，就是新耶路撒冷。─引用经文
二　基督在祂职事的第三个时期中所作的第二件事，就是产生得胜者：
１　因着召会的堕落，几乎所有在基督里的信徒都在他们的旧人里为撒但、罪、世界和肉体所击败。
２ 基督在祂写给堕落召会的七封书信里，呼召失败的信徒，凭祂这七倍加强的灵作祂的得胜者，使他们凭着祂的七倍加强，经历祂生机的救恩。
三　基督在祂职事的第三个时期中所作的第三件事，就是终极完成新耶路撒冷：
１　根据新约的整个启示，基督徒工作的独一目标该是新耶路撒冷，就是神永远经纶的终极目标。
２　召会的堕落，主要的是由于这个事实：几乎所有的基督工人都被岔开，以新耶路撒冷之外的许多事物为他们的目标。
３　因此，在召会的堕落下，要作一个得胜者答应主的呼召，我们就需要胜过一切顶替新耶路撒冷为目标的事物，而以神永远经纶的目标，就是新耶路撒冷，为独一无二且终极无比的目标。
参读　如何作同工与长老，并如何履行同工与长老的义务，第一至三篇；基督的三个时期─成肉体、总括与加强，第一至二章。

TOP-大纲|Outline|对照-听抄-目录
　
　
GENERAL SUBJECT
The Crucial Contents of God's New Testament Economy
Message Six
The Full Ministry of Christ in Three Stages— Incarnation, Inclusion, and Intensification
纲目|对照-听抄-目录
I.　The first stage of the full ministry of Christ is the stage of His incarnation, the stage of Christ in the flesh, from His human birth through His human living to His death:
A.　In His incarnation, Christ brought the infinite God into the finite man; He also united and mingled the Triune God with the tripartite man.
B.　In His human living, Christ expressed in His humanity the bountiful God in His rich attributes through His aromatic virtues:
1.　Christ expressed the bountiful God in His human living, mainly expressing God in His rich attributes.
2.　Christ attracted and captivated people through His aromatic virtues:
a.　Not by living His human life in the flesh.
b.　But by living His divine life in resurrection.
C.　In His death, Christ accomplished His all-inclusive judicial redemption:
1.　He terminated all things of the old creation.
2.　He redeemed all the things created by God and fallen in sin—Heb. 2:9; Col. 1:20.
3.　He created (conceived) the new man with His divine element—Eph. 2:15.
4.　He released His divine life from the shell of His humanity—John 12:24.
5.　He laid a foundation for His organic salvation and set up the procedure to attain His ministry in the stage of His inclusion.
II.　The second stage of the full ministry of Christ is the stage of His inclusion, the stage of Christ as the life-giving Spirit, from His resurrection to the degradation of the church:
A.　In His resurrection, Christ was begotten as God's firstborn Son—Acts 13:33:
1.　From eternity past without beginning, Christ was God's only begotten Son, possessing only divinity, without humanity, and not having passed through death into resurrection.
2.　In incarnation the only begotten Son of God became flesh to be a God-man, a man possessing both the divine nature and the human nature.
3.　Through death and resurrection Christ in the flesh as the seed of David was designated to be the firstborn Son of God—Rom. 1:3-4:
a.　In death His humanity was crucified.
b.　In resurrection His crucified humanity was made alive in the Spirit of His divinity (1 Pet. 3:18) and was uplifted into the sonship of the only begotten Son of God.
c.　Thus, He was begotten by God in His resurrection to be the firstborn Son of God.
B.　In His resurrection, Christ as the last Adam became the life-giving Spirit—1 Cor. 15:45b:
1.　Christ, the Son of God as the second of the Divine Trinity, after completing His ministry on the earth, became (was transfigured into) the life-giving Spirit in His resurrection.
2.　Christ's becoming the life-giving Spirit was for the release of the divine life that was confined in the shell of His humanity and for the dispensing of this life into His believers, making them the many members which constitute His Body—John 12:24.
3.　This life-giving Spirit who is the pneumatic Christ is also called the Spirit of life (Rom. 8:2), the Spirit of Jesus (Acts 16:7), the Spirit of Christ (Rom 8:9), the Spirit of Jesus Christ (Phil. 1:19), and the Lord Spirit (2 Cor. 3:18).
C.　In His resurrection, Christ regenerated the believers for His Body—1 Pet. 1:3:
1.　The pneumatic Christ became the firstborn Son of God and the life-giving Spirit for the regenerating of the believers, making them the many sons of God born of God with Him in the one universal great delivery:
a.　For the composition of the house of God, even the household of God.
b.　For the constitution of the Body of Christ to be His fullness, His expression and expansion, to consummate the eternal expression and expansion of the processed and consummated Triune God.
2.　The Christ in resurrection gives Himself as the all-inclusive life-giving Spirit without measure through His speaking of the words of God—John 3:34.
3.　All the believers in Christ are built up into a dwelling place of God in their spirit indwelt by Him as the Spirit (Eph. 2:22) through dispositional sanctification (Rom. 15:16), renewing (Titus 3:5), transformation (2 Cor. 3:18), and conformation (Rom. 8:29).
III.　The third stage of the full ministry of Christ is the stage of His intensification, the stage of Christ as the sevenfold intensified Spirit, from the degradation of the church to the consummation of the New Jerusalem:
A.　The first thing which Christ is doing in the third stage of His ministry is to intensify His organic salvation:
1.　On the way of Christ's ministry in the stage of His inclusion, which is to carry out His organic salvation for the producing of the church and the building up of His Body to consummate the New Jerusalem, the church became degraded, frustrating the accomplishment of God's eternal economy.
2.　Hence, Christ became the sevenfold intensified Spirit (Rev. 1:4; 4:5; 5:6; 3:1) to intensify His organic salvation sevenfold for the building up of His Body to consummate God's eternal goal—the New Jerusalem.
B.　The second thing which Christ is doing in the third stage of His ministry is to produce the overcomers:
1.　Through the degradation of the church nearly all the believers in Christ became defeated in their old man by Satan, sin, the world, and their flesh.
2.　In His seven epistles to the degraded churches, Christ calls the defeated believers to be His overcomers by Himself as the sevenfold intensified Spirit for their experience of His organic salvation in His sevenfold intensification.
C.　The third thing which Christ is doing in the third stage of His ministry is to consummate the New Jerusalem:
1.　According to the entire revelation of the New Testament, the unique goal of the Christian work should be the New Jerusalem, which is the ultimate goal of God's eternal economy.
2.　The degradation of the church is mainly due to the fact that nearly all the Christian workers are distracted to take many things other than the New Jerusalem as their goal.
3.　Hence, to be overcomers answering the Lord's call under the degradation of the church, we need to overcome all the things which replace the New Jerusalem as the goal and take the goal of God's eternal economy, that is, the New Jerusalem, as our unique and ultimate goal.

TOP-纲目|对照-听抄-目录
　
　
第六篇　基督在三个时期中丰满的职事─成肉体、总括与加强
The Full Ministry of Christ in Three Stages— Incarnation, Inclusion, and Intensification
纲目|outline-听抄-目录
壹　基督丰满职事的第一个时期，是祂成肉体的时期，就是基督在肉体里的时期，从祂的出生，经过祂的人性生活，到祂的死：
I.　The first stage of the full ministry of Christ is the stage of His incarnation, the stage of Christ in the flesh, from His human birth through His human living to His death:
一　在祂的成肉体里，基督将无限的神带到有限的人里面；祂也将三一神与三部分人联结并调和一起。
A.　In His incarnation, Christ brought the infinite God into the finite man; He also united and mingled the Triune God with the tripartite man.
二　在祂的人性生活里，基督借着祂芬芳的美德，在祂的人性里彰显全备之神丰富的属性：
B.　In His human living, Christ expressed in His humanity the bountiful God in His rich attributes through His aromatic virtues:
１　基督在祂人性生活中彰显全备的神，主要的是彰显神丰富的属性。
1.　Christ expressed the bountiful God in His human living, mainly expressing God in His rich attributes.
２　基督借着祂芬芳的美德吸引并夺取人：
2.　Christ attracted and captivated people through His aromatic virtues:
a　不是在祂的肉体里，凭祂人性的生命活着。
a.　Not by living His human life in the flesh.
b　乃是在祂的复活中，凭祂神圣的生命活着。
b.　But by living His divine life in resurrection.
三　在祂的死里，基督完成祂包罗万有之法理的救赎：
C.　In His death, Christ accomplished His all-inclusive judicial redemption:
１　祂了结一切旧造的东西。
1.　He terminated all things of the old creation.
２　祂救赎神所创造、却堕落在罪中的一切东西─来二9，西一20。
2.　He redeemed all the things created by God and fallen in sin—Heb. 2:9; Col. 1:20.
３　祂用祂神圣的元素创造（孕育）新人─弗二15。
3.　He created (conceived) the new man with His divine element—Eph. 2:15.
４　祂从祂人性的体壳里，将祂神圣的生命释放出来─约十二24。
4.　He released His divine life from the shell of His humanity—John 12:24.
５　祂为祂生机的救恩立下根基，并且设定达成祂在总括时期中之职事的手续。
5.　He laid a foundation for His organic salvation and set up the procedure to attain His ministry in the stage of His inclusion.
贰　基督丰满职事的第二个时期，是祂总括的时期，就是基督成为赐生命之灵的时期，从祂的复活到召会的堕落：
II.　The second stage of the full ministry of Christ is the stage of His inclusion, the stage of Christ as the life-giving Spirit, from His resurrection to the degradation of the church:
一　在祂的复活中，基督生为神的长子─徒十三33：
A.　In His resurrection, Christ was begotten as God's firstborn Son—Acts 13:33:
１　从已过无始的永远，基督就是神的独生子，只具有神性，并无人性，也没有经过死而进入复活。
1.　From eternity past without beginning, Christ was God's only begotten Son, possessing only divinity, without humanity, and not having passed through death into resurrection.
２　神的独生子在成肉体时，化身成为一个神人，就是一个兼有神人二性的人。
2.　In incarnation the only begotten Son of God became flesh to be a God-man, a man possessing both the divine nature and the human nature.
３　基督在肉体里作大卫的后裔，借着死与复活，被标出为神的儿子─罗一3～4：
3.　Through death and resurrection Christ in the flesh as the seed of David was designated to be the firstborn Son of God—Rom. 1:3-4:
a　在死里，祂的人性被钉十字架。
a.　In death His humanity was crucified.
b　在复活中，祂被钉死的人性被祂神性的灵所点活，（彼前三18，）并且被提高到神独生子之儿子名分里。─引用经文
b.　In resurrection His crucified humanity was made alive in the Spirit of His divinity (1 Pet. 3:18) and was uplifted into the sonship of the only begotten Son of God.
c　因此，祂在复活中被神生为神的长子。
c.　Thus, He was begotten by God in His resurrection to be the firstborn Son of God.
二　在祂的复活中，末后的亚当基督成为赐生命的灵─林前十五45下：
B.　In His resurrection, Christ as the last Adam became the life-giving Spirit—1 Cor. 15:45b:
１　神的儿子基督，就是神圣三一的第二者，完成祂在地上的职事之后，在复活中成了，就是改变形状而成为赐生命的灵。
1.　Christ, the Son of God as the second of the Divine Trinity, after completing His ministry on the earth, became (was transfigured into) the life-giving Spirit in His resurrection.
２　基督成为赐生命的灵，乃是为要将那局限在基督人性体壳里的神圣生命释放出来，并将其分赐到祂的信徒里面，使他们成为构成祂身体的许多肢体─约十二24。
2.　Christ's becoming the life-giving Spirit was for the release of the divine life that was confined in the shell of His humanity and for the dispensing of this life into His believers, making them the many members which constitute His Body—John 12:24.
３　这赐生命的灵就是那是灵的基督，也称为生命的灵，（罗八2，）耶稣的灵，（徒十六7，）基督的灵，（罗八9，）耶稣基督的灵，（腓一19，）主灵。（林后三18）。─引用经文
3.　This life-giving Spirit who is the pneumatic Christ is also called the Spirit of life (Rom. 8:2), the Spirit of Jesus (Acts 16:7), the Spirit of Christ (Rom 8:9), the Spirit of Jesus Christ (Phil. 1:19), and the Lord Spirit (2 Cor. 3:18).
三　在祂的复活中，基督为着祂的身体重生信徒─彼前一3：
C.　In His resurrection, Christ regenerated the believers for His Body—1 Pet. 1:3:
１　那是灵的基督成了神的长子和赐生命的灵，为着重生信徒，使他们成为神的许多儿子，与祂在一个宇宙的大生产中一同由神所生：
1.　The pneumatic Christ became the firstborn Son of God and the life-giving Spirit for the regenerating of the believers, making them the many sons of God born of God with Him in the one universal great delivery:
a　为着组成神的家，就是神的家人。
a.　For the composition of the house of God, even the household of God.
b　为着构成基督的身体作祂的丰满，就是祂的彰显和扩展，以完成经过过程并终极完成之三一神永远的彰显和扩展。
b.　For the constitution of the Body of Christ to be His fullness, His expression and expansion, to consummate the eternal expression and expansion of the processed and consummated Triune God.
２　基督在复活里借着说神的话，没有限量的将祂自己这包罗万有、赐生命的灵赐给人─约三34。
2.　The Christ in resurrection gives Himself as the all-inclusive life-giving Spirit without measure through His speaking of the words of God—John 3:34.
３　所有在基督里的信徒都被建造，成为神在他们由祂的灵内住之灵里的居所，（弗二22，）这乃是借着在性质上的圣别、（罗十五16、）更新、（多三5、）变化、（林后三18）和模成。（罗八29。）─引用经文
3.　All the believers in Christ are built up into a dwelling place of God in their spirit indwelt by Him as the Spirit (Eph. 2:22) through dispositional sanctification (Rom. 15:16), renewing (Titus 3:5), transformation (2 Cor. 3:18), and conformation (Rom. 8:29).
叁　基督丰满职事的第三个时期，是祂加强的时期，就是基督是七倍加强之灵的时期，从召会的堕落到新耶路撒冷的终极完成：
III.　The third stage of the full ministry of Christ is the stage of His intensification, the stage of Christ as the sevenfold intensified Spirit, from the degradation of the church to the consummation of the New Jerusalem:
一　基督在祂职事的第三个时期中所作的第一件事，就是加强祂生机的救恩：
A.　The first thing which Christ is doing in the third stage of His ministry is to intensify His organic salvation:
１　基督在祂总括时期中，要完成祂生机的救恩，为着产生召会，建造基督的身体，以终极完成新耶路撒冷，但在这时期之职事的中途，召会堕落了，阻扰神永远经纶的完成。
1.　On the way of Christ's ministry in the stage of His inclusion, which is to carry out His organic salvation for the producing of the church and the building up of His Body to consummate the New Jerusalem, the church became degraded, frustrating the accomplishment of God's eternal economy.
２　因此，基督成了七倍加强的灵，（启一4，四5，五6，三1，）要七倍的加强神生机的救恩，为着建造基督的身体，以终极完成神永远的目标，就是新耶路撒冷。─引用经文
2.　Hence, Christ became the sevenfold intensified Spirit (Rev. 1:4; 4:5; 5:6; 3:1) to intensify His organic salvation sevenfold for the building up of His Body to consummate God's eternal goal—the New Jerusalem.
二　基督在祂职事的第三个时期中所作的第二件事，就是产生得胜者：
B.　The second thing which Christ is doing in the third stage of His ministry is to produce the overcomers:
１　因着召会的堕落，几乎所有在基督里的信徒都在他们的旧人里为撒但、罪、世界和肉体所击败。
1.　Through the degradation of the church nearly all the believers in Christ became defeated in their old man by Satan, sin, the world, and their flesh.
２ 基督在祂写给堕落召会的七封书信里，呼召失败的信徒，凭祂这七倍加强的灵作祂的得胜者，使他们凭着祂的七倍加强，经历祂生机的救恩。
2.　In His seven epistles to the degraded churches, Christ calls the defeated believers to be His overcomers by Himself as the sevenfold intensified Spirit for their experience of His organic salvation in His sevenfold intensification.
三　基督在祂职事的第三个时期中所作的第三件事，就是终极完成新耶路撒冷：
C.　The third thing which Christ is doing in the third stage of His ministry is to consummate the New Jerusalem:
１　根据新约的整个启示，基督徒工作的独一目标该是新耶路撒冷，就是神永远经纶的终极目标。
1.　According to the entire revelation of the New Testament, the unique goal of the Christian work should be the New Jerusalem, which is the ultimate goal of God's eternal economy.
２　召会的堕落，主要的是由于这个事实：几乎所有的基督工人都被岔开，以新耶路撒冷之外的许多事物为他们的目标。
2.　The degradation of the church is mainly due to the fact that nearly all the Christian workers are distracted to take many things other than the New Jerusalem as their goal.
３　因此，在召会的堕落下，要作一个得胜者答应主的呼召，我们就需要胜过一切顶替新耶路撒冷为目标的事物，而以神永远经纶的目标，就是新耶路撒冷，为独一无二且终极无比的目标。
3.　Hence, to be overcomers answering the Lord's call under the degradation of the church, we need to overcome all the things which replace the New Jerusalem as the goal and take the goal of God's eternal economy, that is, the New Jerusalem, as our unique and ultimate goal.

TOP-纲目|outline-听抄-目录
　
　
MESSAGE SIX
THE FULL MINISTRY OF CHRIST IN THREE STAGES— INCARNATION, INCLUSION, AND INTENSIFICATION
纲目|Outline|对照-目录
（本文为英文听抄扫描所得，未经校对）
The full ministry of Christ in three stages was first released through the ministry of Brother Lee in April and June of 1996. The messages given at that time are published in Incarnation, Inclusion, and Intensification. The first three messages of How to Be a Co-worker and an Elder and How to Fulfill Their Obligations, given in October 1996, are a full unveiling of this marvelous truth. By His full ministry in three stages Christ accomplishes in full God's eternal economy to build up the Body of Christ and consummate the New Jerusalem. How the Lord's recovery will be and how it will go on depend on how we handle the teaching of the full ministry of Christ in His three divine and mystical stages. We need to learn how to nourish people by ministering Christ to them in His full ministry in three stages. Therefore, this is a part of the crucial contents of the New Testament ministry.
THE FIRST STAGE OF THE FULL MINISTRY OF CHRIST IS THE STAGE OF HIS INCARNATION, THE STAGE OF CHRIST IN THE FLESH, FROM HIS HUMAN BIRTH THROUGH HIS HUMAN LIVING TO HIS DEATH
The first stage of the full ministry of Christ is the stage of His incarnation, the stage of Christ in the flesh, from His human birth through His human living to His death. This stage comprises three major items: the human birth of Christ, the human living of Christ, and the death of Christ. In each of these matters Christ accomplished something marvelous for the carrying out of God's eternal economy.
In His Incarnation, Christ Brought the Infinite God into the Finite Man; He Also United and Mingled the Triune God with the Tripartite Man
In His incarnation, Christ brought the infinite God into the finite man; He also united and mingled the Triune God with the tripartite man. God is infinite. He fills the whole universe, and He is bigger than the universe. Man, however, is finite, but in the incarnation, Christ brought the infinite God into a finite man. This is a wonder of wonders and a mystery of mysteries. This is what the Lord accomplished through His incarnation. Colossians 2:9 says that all the fullness of the Godhead dwells in Christ bodily. The fullness of the Triune God dwelt in a human body. To be sure, a human body is finite, yet in the human body of the Lord Jesus the fullness of the Triune Godhead dwelt, and in His resurrected body it still dwells now and forever. This is a marvelous thing that the Lord accomplished. Before the incarnation of Christ, God and man were separate. God was not in man; He was outside of man, but in the incarnation the infinite God entered into the finite man.
The Triune God also united and mingled Himself with the tripartite man. Before the incarnation, God and man were not one, but in the incarnation of Christ, God and man became one. They were united, and they were mingled together to be one God-man, the Lord Jesus Christ, the first God-man who lived on the earth. He was the mingling of divinity with humanity, but in this mingling the characteristics of His divinity and His humanity were not confused. His divinity and humanity remained distinct, but they were blended and mingled together in one person. God's economy is to join Himself to man, to mingle Himself with man, and ultimately to incorporate Himself with man to be one universal incorporation. Therefore, the incarnation was crucial for the carrying out of God's eternal economy. It was the beginning of the process to mingle together God and man and incorporate them into one.
In His Human Living, Christ Expressed in His Humanity the Bountiful God in His Rich Attributes through His Aromatic Virtues
After His birth, Christ lived a human life on the earth for thirty-three and a half years in which He accomplished something extraordinary. In His human living, Christ expressed in His humanity the bountiful God in His rich attributes through His aromatic virtues. This is the new vocabulary in the Lord's recovery, which we all need to learn.
Christ Expressed the Bountiful God in His Human Living, Mainly Expressing God in His Rich Attributes
Christ expressed the bountiful God in His human living, mainly expressing God in His rich attributes. All the virtues of Christ were aromatic. That means that they were sweet and full of fragrance. When we read the four Gospels, we see the human living of the Lord Jesus. It was extraordinary, unexplainable, and indescribable because in the human living of Jesus the rich attributes of the bountiful God were expressed in the aromatic virtues of Christ as a God-man. He was living a human life on the earth, but in His human virtues God's attributes were expressed. This made all His virtues aromatic, sweet, and fragrant. In the four Gospels we encounter a sweet and fragrant person.
God's attributes are the unsearchable riches of what He is. God is a composition of all His divine attributes. God is love, God is light, God is holiness, and God is righteousness. God has many attributes, and all these attributes are rich. God created man in His own image and in Llis own likeness, giving man virtues that correspond to His attributes. His desire is that all His divine attributes would be mingled with man's virtues and become the reality of man's human virtues to be expressed through his virtues. This makes man's virtues aromatic. As the first God-man, Christ expressed the attributes of God. God wants all His attributes to be expressed through human virtues, and the Lord Jesus in His human living accomplished this wonderful purpose.
Christ Attracted and Captivated People through His Aromatic Virtues
Because He expressed God's attributes in His aromatic virtues, Christ attracted and captivated people through His aromatic virtues. He was able to attract people to Himself and captivate and gain them to follow Him. When the Lord saw the disciples, He called them simply by saying, "Follow Me." He did not say much to them, but there must have been something so aromatic in Him that made them willing to leave everything to follow Him. They were attracted and captivated by Him, so they followed this wonderful aromatic person who was so fragrant and attractive. Today we are no different from the disciples. The Lord has called us, and we have been attracted and captured by Him. We are following Him because He is so attractive, fragrant, and captivating to us.
Christ could captivate people in such a way because He lived His human life not by living in the flesh but by living His divine life in resurrection. This is a precious revelation given to us in the New Testament ministry. We all know that the Lord was an extraordinary person, but what made Him extraodinary? It was the way He lived. His human life was perfect and without any sin. There was no element of sin in His humanity, yet He did not live by His sinless human life. He lived the divine life in resurrection. Even before He was crucified, He lived in resurrection because He lived the divine life. In this living God's attributes became the reality and the content of His human virtues, so He expressed God's attributes in His human virtues.
The human living of Christ is a real pattern for us. By our enjoyment of Him, we should live the way He lived. By eating and drinking Him we are supplied with His riches and are enabled to live a life that is not by the human life but by the divine life in resurrection to manifest the attributes of God in aromatic virtues. In describing the New Testament ministry, Paul said that the New Testament ministers are captives of Christ led by God in a procession to celebrate the victory of Christ, and they become a fragrance of Christ (2 Cor. 2:14-15). Wherever they went, they scattered Christ as the sweet incense in their ministry. This shows that we also can live this kind of life and become this kind of person. This is what God desires. He wants us to live the divine life in resurrection, not to live the human life in the flesh, so that His divine attributes can be expressed in our human virtues. This is the wonderful human living of the Lord Jesus.
In His Death, Christ Accomplished His All-inclusive Judicial Redemption
In His death, Christ accomplished His all-inclusive judicial redemption. At the end of His human life He accomplished a marvelous and all-inclusive death in which He accomplished His all-inclusive judicial redemption. This was the last item of His ministry in the stage of His incarnation.
He Terminated All Things of the Old Creation and He Redeemed All the Things Created by God and Fallen in Sin
In His death, He terminated all things of the old creation. It was not only Christ who died on the cross; everything in the old creation was terminated by the all-inclusive death of Christ. Through His death, He also redeemed all the things created by God and fallen in sin (Heb. 2:9; Col. 1:20). Christ's marvelous death was all-terminating and all-redeeming.
He Created (Conceived) the New Man with His Divine Element
In His death, He created (conceived) the new man with His divine element (Eph. 2:15). Christ's death was the new man-creating death. He created and blended, in Himself as the sphere and element, the lews and the Gentiles into one new man. The new man was conceived on the cross, and he was born in the resurrection of Christ to be a new child with Christ as the Head and the church as the Body.
